## The USGS warning system that knows when rumbling volcanoes will blow their mountain tops
 - [https://www.engadget.com/the-usgs-warning-system-that-knows-when-rumbling-volcanoes-will-blow-their-mountain-tops-004544614.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/the-usgs-warning-system-that-knows-when-rumbling-volcanoes-will-blow-their-mountain-tops-004544614.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 23:45:44+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>More than 120 volcanic eruptions have occurred in the United States in the 42 years since Mount St. Helens erupted over Washington in 1980, killing 57 and inflicting over a billion dollars in property damage. While none have been nearly as destructive, their mere presence can impact <a href="https://www.businessinsider.com/klm-flight-amsterdam-return-11-hour-volcano-mexico-schiphol-2019-11">human activities</a> and even <a href="https://eos.org/science-updates/working-together-toward-better-volcanic-forecasting">economies</a> hundreds of miles away. Altogether the <a href="https://pubs.usgs.gov/sir/2018/5140/sir20185140.pdf">US Geological Survey (USGS) has identified</a> 161 geologically active volcanoes in 14 states and territories, a third of which constitute “high” or “very high” threats to their surrounding communities, and another 58 volcanoes nationwide <a href="https://pubs.usgs.gov/of/2005/1164/2005-1164.pdf">classified as being undermonitored</a>. The agency operates five volcano monitoring stations along the west coast to keep an eye on all but the least dangerous as part of the Survey’s <a href="https://volcanoes.usgs.gov/index.html">Volcano Hazards Program</a>. On average, around 60 volcanoes erupt annually, as Hawaii’s Mauna Loa is doing right now.</p><p>Mauna Loa, which had stood dormant for the past 38 years, <a href="https://www.hawaiinewsnow.com/2022/11/28/mauna-loa-eruption-underway-lava-currently-contained-summit/">reawakened late Sunday night</a> for the eighth time since 1843. “Lava flows are not threatening any downslope communities and all indications are that the eruption will remain in the Northeast Rift Zone,” reads <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/volcanoes/mauna-loa/volcano-updates">Monday’s red alert update from the USGS Hawaiian Volcano Observatory</a> (HVO). “Volcanic gas and possibly fine ash and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pele%27s_hair">Pele's Hair</a> may be carried downwind. Residents at risk from Mauna Loa lava flows should review preparedness and refer to <a href="https://www.hawaiicounty.gov/departments/civil-defense/active-civil-defense-alerts-and-maps.">Hawai‘i County Civil Defense information for further guidance</a>.” This week’s eruption is decidedly mild compared to 2018’s Kīlauea Volcano event that destroyed 700 homes and launched ash 3,000 meters into the atmosphere, <a href="https://www.cntraveler.com/story/hawaiis-kilauea-volcano-erupts-with-ash-puts-airlines-on-red-alert">where it disrupted air traffic patterns</a>.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>While lava receives a majority of the public attention, volcanoes have myriad methods for ruining your week with fire and (literal) brimstone. Volcanic ash can travel miles into the stratosphere before raining back down where it <a href="https://volcanoes.usgs.gov/volcanic_ash/health.html">exacerbates chronic lung diseases like asthma and emphysema</a>; carbon dioxide and hydrogen sulfide <a href="https://www.cdc.gov/disasters/volcanoes/facts.html">collect in low-lying areas to suffocate the unwary</a> and seismic shifts resulting from the initial explosion can trigger landslides, tsunamis, floods, and large-scale power outages.</p><p>“Unlike many other natural disasters … volcanic eruptions can be predicted well in advance of their occurrence if adequate in-ground instrumentation is in place that allows earliest detection of unrest, providing the time needed to mitigate the worst of their effects,” David Applegate, USGS associate director for natural hazards, <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/congressional-statement/statement-david-applegate-associate-director-natural-hazards-us-geological">told a House subcommittee in 2017</a>.</p><p>As <a href="https://eos.org/articles/national-volcano-warning-system-gains-steam"><em>Eos</em></a> magazine points out, nobody died as a result of the 2018 Kīlauea eruption, in large part due to the efforts of monitors at the HVO. But, <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/publications/2018-update-us-geological-survey-national-volcanic-threat-assessment">a 2018 threat assessment</a> found that, out of the 18 volcanoes listed as “very high” threat, only three — Mauna Loa, St Helens and the <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/volcanoes/long-valley-caldera">Long Valley Caldera</a> — were rated as “well monitored” when that eruption was happening.</p><p>On the same day that Kīlauea blew its top, the US Senate unanimously passed <a href="https://www.congress.gov/bill/115th-congress/senate-bill/346">S.346</a>, establishing the <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/programs/VHP/national-volcano-early-warning-system-monitoring-volcanoes-according-their-threat">National Volcano Early Warning and Monitoring System</a> (NVEWS). The following March, the House of Representatives passed its version, PL 116-9/S.47, dubbed the <a href="https://www.congress.gov/116/plaws/publ9/PLAW-116publ9.pdf">John D. Dingell Jr. Conservation, Management, and Recreation Act</a>. Not unlike California’s new <a href="https://www.engadget.com/usgs-earthquake-early-warning-system-west-coast-mobile-alerts-170918179.html">ShakeAlert</a> early earthquake warning scheme, the NVEWS works to combine and standardize the existing hodgepodge of (<a href="https://www.usgs.gov/news/featured-story/national-volcano-early-warning-system-nvews-will-help-usgs-better-monitor">often outdated</a>) volcano monitoring hardware operated by both government agencies and academic organizations <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/programs/VHP/national-volcano-early-warning-system-monitoring-volcanoes-according-their-threat">into a unified system</a>, “to ensure that the most hazardous volcanoes will be properly monitored well in advance of the onset of activity.”</p><figure><img alt="A clipart picture of a stylized voplcano surrounded by cameras, seismic, GOPS, tiltmeter and thermal imaging sensors" src="https://s.yimg.com/os/creatr-uploaded-images/2022-11/bc8c0f00-6f6c-11ed-b7ff-c37cf50ccf81" /><figcaption></figcaption><div class="photo-credit">USGS</div></figure><p>“Improvements to volcano monitoring networks allow the USGS to detect volcanic unrest at the earliest possible stage,” Tom Murray, USGS Volcano Science Center director, said in a <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/news/featured-story/national-volcano-early-warning-system-nvews-will-help-usgs-better-monitor">2018 USGS release</a>. “This provides more time to issue forecasts and warnings of hazardous volcanic activity and gives at-risk communities more time to prepare.”</p><p>The NVEWS Act, which was sponsored by Senator Lisa Murkowski (R - AK), earmarks $55 million annually between 2019 and 2023 to provide more accurate and timely eruption forecasts by increasing partnerships with local governments and proactively sharing data with the volcano science community. It also seeks to increase staffing and systems — from broadband seismometers, infrasound arrays, and real-time continuous GPS receivers, to streaming webcams, satellite overwatch and volcanic gas sensors — for 24/7 volcano monitoring and establishes a grant system for furthering volcanology research.</p><figure><img alt="lots of words and numbers" src="https://s.yimg.com/os/creatr-uploaded-images/2022-11/fc598630-6f6c-11ed-bfb5-4dcc7abe716c" /><figcaption></figcaption><div class="photo-credit">USGS</div></figure><p>The USGS ranks volcanic threats based on the risk they pose to public health and property — essentially how potentially destructive the volcano itself is in relation to how many people and things might be impacted when it does erupt. The USGS assigns numerical values to the <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/publications/2018-update-us-geological-survey-national-volcanic-threat-assessment">24 various hazard and exposure factors</a> for each volcano, then combined to calculate the overall threat score which is divided into five levels (like DEFCONs!). High and Very High get the most detailed monitoring coverage because duh, Moderate threat volcanoes still receive real-time monitoring but don’t have <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsImxhbmRpbmdVcmwiOiJodHRwczovL3d3dy55b3V0dWJlLmNvbS93YXRjaD92PU1ETjE4eUhFdjJJIiwiY29udGVudFV1aWQiOiI2MDQ2MjY3Ni1lY2U2LTQxMzktYWIwMC00MzIyMGNlMGYwMzYifQ&amp;signature=AQAAAQmx1fXsz3MPH6kztmPEOKqBtINLAimp41uULkCz3hUT&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.youtube.com%2Fwatch%3Fv%3DMDN18yHEv2I">Tommy Lee Jones standing by to intercede</a>, and Low (and Very Low) get checked on as needed. As of May 2022, when the USGS submitted its second annual NVEWS report to Congress, <a href="https://sgp.fas.org/crs/homesec/IF11987.pdf">the USGS had spent just under half</a> of the money appropriated for FY 2021 with the funds going to activities like installing a net-gen <a href="https://www.usgs.gov/programs/VHP/usgs-developed-lahar-detection-systems-provide-warning-lahars">lahar detection system</a> on Mount Rainier, upgrading the telemetry for more than two dozen observation posts throughout Alaska, Oregon, Washington, California and Hawaii.</p>

## Google sued by FTC and seven states over 'deceptive' Pixel 4 ads
 - [https://www.engadget.com/google-iheartmedia-pixel-4-deceptive-ads-lawsuit-210535824.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/google-iheartmedia-pixel-4-deceptive-ads-lawsuit-210535824.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 21:05:35+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>You're not the only one wondering if that social media star really used a hot new phone. The Federal Trade Commission and seven states <a href="https://www.ftc.gov/news-events/news/press-releases/2022/11/ftc-seven-states-sue-google-iheartmedia-deceptive-ads-promoting-pixel-4-smartphone">have sued</a> Google and iHeartMedia for running allegedly "deceptive" <a href="https://www.engadget.com/2019-10-21-google-pixel-4-and-4-xl-review-motion-sense-cameras.html">Pixel 4</a> ads. Promos aired between 2019 and 2020 featured influencers that extolled the features of phones they reportedly didn't own — Google didn't even supply Pixels before most of the ads were recorded, officials said.</p><p>iHeartMedia and 11 other radio networks ran the Pixel 4 ads in ten large markets. They aired about 29,000 times. It's not clear how many people listened to the commercials.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>The FTC aims to bar Google and iHeartMedia from making any future misleading claims about ownership. It also asks both companies to prove their compliance through reports. The states, including Arizona, California, Georgia, Illinois, Massachusetts, New York and Texas, have also issued judgments demanding the firms pay $9.4 million in penalties.</p><p>Google spokesperson José Castañeda told Engadget in a statement that the company was "pleased" to address the situation and took advertising laws "seriously." He added that Google didn't see this as a lawsuit (it's technically a proposed FTC order and state judgments), and that the tech giant was only settling with six out of the seven states.</p><p>Misrepresentative phone ads are far from new. <a href="https://www.engadget.com/2018-08-20-huawei-caught-passing-off-dlsr-pictures-as-phone-camera-samples.html">Huawei</a> and <a href="https://www.engadget.com/2018-12-04-samsung-uses-dslr-photo-to-sell-galaxy-a8-star-camera.html">Samsung</a> have both been caught passing off stock DSLR photos as representative of their phone cameras. There's also a history of celebrities marketing phones it's not clear they use. Gal Gadot had to <a href="https://www.cnet.com/tech/mobile/gal-gadot-says-she-didnt-cheat-on-huawei-mate-10-pro-with-iphone/">defend</a> herself against claims she pitched Huawei phones while posting on Twitter from an iPhone, for instance (it was her publicist).</p><p>However, the accusations here are more serious. The FTC and participating states are contending that Google set out to use false testimonials. It had a "blatant disrespect" for truth-in-ads rules, according to FTC consumer protection director Samuel Levine.  While the punishment is tiny compared to the <a href="https://www.engadget.com/google-fails-to-overturn-eu-android-antitrust-ruling-085808140.html">antitrust   penalties</a> Google has faced so far, it could damage trust in the company's campaigns for <a href="https://www.engadget.com/google-pixel-7-and-pixel-7-pro-review-still-the-best-bargain-in-flagship-phones-170031940.html">newer Pixels</a> and other hardware.</p>

## Elon Musk claims Apple has 'threatened to withhold’ Twitter from the App Store
 - [https://www.engadget.com/elon-musk-apple-threatened-to-withhold-twitter-from-app-store-204205794.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/elon-musk-apple-threatened-to-withhold-twitter-from-app-store-204205794.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 20:42:05+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>Elon Musk has taken aim at Apple’s App Store policies amid claims that the company has “threatened to withhold” Twitter from its store. According to Musk, Apple “won’t tell us why” it has an issues with Twitter, but the threats have</p><p>In subsequent tweets, Musk railed against Apple’s 30 percent “tax” on in-app purchases, and claimed the App Store owner has “censored” other developers. He also<a href="https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1597285572699074560"><ins> said</ins></a> that Apple “has mostly stopped advertising on Twitter.” (Apple wouldn’t be <a href="https://www.engadget.com/twitter-losing-advertisers-boycott-193748977.html"><ins>the first</ins></a> major advertiser to do so in recent weeks.)</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><div id="05080408d697412a9348b46631d044ea"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">Apple has also threatened to withhold Twitter from its App Store, but won’t tell us why</p>— Elon Musk (@elonmusk) <a href="https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1597300125243944961?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">November 28, 2022</a></blockquote></div><p>This  wouldn’t be the first time Apple has taken issue with Twitter. In an op-ed recently <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?merchantId=c813ae39-7d58-41cb-ac66-ad830606ceef&amp;siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;merchantName=The+New+York+Times&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsInN0b3JlSWQiOiJjODEzYWUzOS03ZDU4LTQxY2ItYWM2Ni1hZDgzMDYwNmNlZWYiLCJsYW5kaW5nVXJsIjoiaHR0cHM6Ly93d3cubnl0aW1lcy5jb20vMjAyMi8xMS8xOC9vcGluaW9uL3R3aXR0ZXIteW9lbC1yb3RoLWVsb24tbXVzay5odG1sIiwiY29udGVudFV1aWQiOiI1ZjEwMDkxNy1hZjIwLTRkMjgtOGRlNC1iMzc5YmNlMzFiOGMifQ&amp;signature=AQAAAY77DzwlTnkXsemiz0F-gFcwaqzj6So419PfBm3_lHUG&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nytimes.com%2F2022%2F11%2F18%2Fopinion%2Ftwitter-yoel-roth-elon-musk.html"><ins>published by</ins></a><em>The New York Times</em>, Twitter’s former head of trust and safety, Yoel Roth, said that Apple’s App Store reviewers often flagged content on Twitter during its app review process.</p><p>“In my time at Twitter, representatives of the app stores regularly raised concerns about content available on our platform,” Roth wrote, saying that app reviewers had flagged instances of racial slurs and nudity on the service. “Even as they appear to be driven largely by manual checks and anecdotes, these review procedures have the power to derail company plans and trigger all-hands-on-deck crises for weeks or months at a time.”</p><p>Apple didn’t immediately respond to a request for comment.</p><p>Musk didn’t specify if Apple is holding new updates to the service or threatening to remove the app from its store altogether. However, there are a number of recent issues that could have flagged Twitter for additional scrutiny.</p><p>On Sunday, <em>The Guardian</em><a href="https://www.theguardian.com/world/2022/nov/28/twitter-failed-to-detect-upload-of-christchurch-mosque-terror-attack-videos"><ins>reported</ins></a> that Twitter had initially failed to pull “freshly uploaded” video of a 2019 terror attack at a mosque in Christchurch, New Zealand, until government officials alerted the company to its existence. There has also been widespread concern from activists over the rise in <a href="https://www.engadget.com/twitter-removed-1500-accounts-coordinated-trolling-campaign-073056421.html"><ins>hate speech</ins></a> and <a href="https://www.engadget.com/twitter-unbans-jordan-peterson-babylon-bee-kathy-griffin-204407440.html"><ins>reinstatemen</ins></a>t of high-profile accounts who were banned for breaking Twitter’s hate speech policies. Musk also recently stated he planned to give <a href="https://www.engadget.com/twitter-engineers-fired-holiday-pay-amnesty-elon-musk-210356513.html"><ins>“amnesty”</ins></a> to previously-banned accounts.</p><p>Apple has strict, if unevenly enforced, rules that govern the content that can appear in apps in its store.  Parler, a “free speech” rival to Twitter, <a href="https://www.engadget.com/apple-suspends-parler-app-store-014314396.html"><ins>was removed</ins></a> from the App Store for months due to its lax content moderation rules (the app was reinstated after it rolled out an AI-based moderation system). In 2018, Tumblr <a href="https://www.engadget.com/2018-12-13-tumblr-back-on-the-app-store.html"><ins>banned adult</ins></a> content following a brief removal from the App Store.</p>

## Tesla is reportedly redesigning the Model 3 to cut production costs
 - [https://www.engadget.com/tesla-highland-model-3-redesign-report-172945432.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/tesla-highland-model-3-redesign-report-172945432.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 17:29:45+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>Tesla is working on a redesign of the Model 3 codenamed “Highland,” according to <a href="https://www.reuters.com/business/autos-transportation/tesla-readies-revamped-model-3-with-project-highland-sources-2022-11-28/"><em><ins>Reuters</ins></em></a>. The company’s goal is to reportedly reduce the complexity and number of components required to produce the sedan. The redesign could include changes to the car’s exterior and powertrain performance. The project is also said to build on the revamp of the <a href="https://www.engadget.com/tesla-model-s-redesign-interior-221606865.html%5C"><ins>2021 Model S</ins></a>. However, it's unknown if the redesigned Model 3 will feature the controversial steering yoke found in its more expensive sibling.</p><p><em>Reuters</em> reports Tesla’s Shanghai Gigafactory will begin producing the new Model 3  sometime during the third quarter of 2023. The company’s Fremont plant will also make the redesigned sedan. It’s unclear how much Tesla expects to save on the new Model 3, nor whether the company will pass on the cost savings to consumers. Tesla currently makes a profit of about $9,500 for every car it produces. <em>Reuters</em> also makes no mention of whether the refresh will feature the automaker’s next-generation <a href="https://www.engadget.com/tesla-battery-day-25k-ev-231307638.html"><ins>4680 battery cells</ins></a>. In 2020, Elon Musk said the new battery design would enable Tesla to produce a $25,000 electric car within three years.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>It's safe to assume that even if the 2023 timeline is accurate, it could be subject to change. <em>Reuters </em><a href="https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1591092334007287809?s=20&amp;t=3kJLammg_FgIkyjKVovlaw"><ins>hasn’t had the best track record</ins></a> with its Tesla reporting recently, and it’s not like the company is great about sticking to deadlines either. When the automaker first announced the <a href="https://www.engadget.com/2019-11-22-tesla-cybertruck-impressions-ride.html"><ins>Cybertruck</ins></a>, for example, Elon Musk said volume production would start in 2021. That date first slipped to <a href="https://www.engadget.com/tesla-cybertruck-delay-2022-150309858.html"><ins>2022</ins></a> and then <a href="https://www.engadget.com/tesla-cybertruck-2023-elon-musk-071706850.html"><ins>2023</ins></a>.</p>

## Crypto lender BlockFi files for Chapter 11 bankruptcy amid FTX fallout
 - [https://www.engadget.com/crypto-lender-blockfi-files-chapter-11-bankruptcy-ftx-165754720.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/crypto-lender-blockfi-files-chapter-11-bankruptcy-ftx-165754720.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 16:57:54+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>Cryptocurrency lender BlockFi has <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsImxhbmRpbmdVcmwiOiJodHRwczovL2Jsb2NrZmkuY29tL05vdmVtYmVyMjgtQ2xpZW50VXBkYXRlIiwiY29udGVudFV1aWQiOiI0NzYyYzM3Zi0xMzQxLTRmYmEtOTYyYi04OTIzZGJkMzNjYmUifQ&amp;signature=AQAAASZBBygEzYkuc7jm3eHHzAMUkykO5U33q86wSLsytdvZ&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fblockfi.com%2FNovember28-ClientUpdate">filed for Chapter 11 bankruptcy protection</a>. The move comes just over two weeks after BlockFi <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsImxhbmRpbmdVcmwiOiJodHRwczovL2Jsb2NrZmkuY29tL25vdmVtYmVyLTE0LTIwMjItYmxvY2tmaS11cGRhdGUiLCJjb250ZW50VXVpZCI6IjQ3NjJjMzdmLTEzNDEtNGZiYS05NjJiLTg5MjNkYmQzM2NiZSJ9&amp;signature=AQAAAV4rj_2cbN3jZyHNVeW9L3QehsQNs6G5qi4rlc7A7QN4&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fblockfi.com%2Fnovember-14-2022-blockfi-update"><ins>suspended all platform activity</ins></a>, including withdrawals, in the wake of crypto exchange <a href="http://engadget.com/tag/ftx">FTX</a>'s implosion. "Given the lack of clarity on the status of FTX.com, FTX US and Alameda, we are not able to operate business as usual," the company <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsImxhbmRpbmdVcmwiOiJodHRwczovL2Jsb2NrZmkuY29tL05vdmVtYmVyMjgtQ2xpZW50RkFRIiwiY29udGVudFV1aWQiOiI0NzYyYzM3Zi0xMzQxLTRmYmEtOTYyYi04OTIzZGJkMzNjYmUifQ&amp;signature=AQAAAWhZgLQEPt25jBkRgknQ3DANnQdy-CWLUNAunu53ghA0&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fblockfi.com%2FNovember28-ClientFAQ"><ins>said in an FAQ</ins></a>. Withdrawals remain paused.</p><p>"BlockFi’s chapter 11 cases will enable BlockFi to stabilize its business and provide BlockFi with the opportunity to consummate a reorganization that maximizes value for all stakeholders," BlockFi said. "The court-supervised restructuring process is transparent and encourages dialogue between all stakeholders."</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>As with many other players in the industry, BlockFi faced an uncertain future after several crypto companies <a href="https://www.engadget.com/celsius-network-freeze-state-securities-board-investigation-231238212.html"><ins>crumbled in the spring</ins></a>, taking the prices of many cryptocurrencies down with them. Soon after, FTX <a href="https://twitter.com/BlockFiZac/status/1542934040092856321"><ins>agreed</ins></a> to prop up BlockFi with a $400 million credit line. The agreement also gave FTX the option to buy BlockFi for up to $240 million. As <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?merchantId=c813ae39-7d58-41cb-ac66-ad830606ceef&amp;siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;merchantName=The+New+York+Times&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsInN0b3JlSWQiOiJjODEzYWUzOS03ZDU4LTQxY2ItYWM2Ni1hZDgzMDYwNmNlZWYiLCJsYW5kaW5nVXJsIjoiaHR0cHM6Ly93d3cubnl0aW1lcy5jb20vMjAyMi8xMS8yOC9idXNpbmVzcy9ibG9ja2ZpLWJhbmtydXB0Y3ktY3J5cHRvY3VycmVuY3ktZnR4Lmh0bWw_c21pZD10dy1zaGFyZSIsImNvbnRlbnRVdWlkIjoiNDc2MmMzN2YtMTM0MS00ZmJhLTk2MmItODkyM2RiZDMzY2JlIn0&amp;signature=AQAAARsRXgLn39iwRkk4zKQZD5B7QzL0fD_rZSgzyNqHQfNa&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nytimes.com%2F2022%2F11%2F28%2Fbusiness%2Fblockfi-bankruptcy-cryptocurrency-ftx.html%3Fsmid%3Dtw-share"><em><ins>The New York Times</ins></em></a> notes, that meant the companies had close financial ties and FTX's <a href="https://www.engadget.com/ftx-bankruptcy-ceo-sam-bankman-fried-resigns-155552534.html"><ins>collapse into bankruptcy</ins></a> has had a knock-on effect on BlockFi.</p><p>“With the collapse of FTX, the BlockFi management team and board of directors immediately took action to protect clients and the company,” Mark Renzi of Berkeley Research Group, BlockFi's financial advisor, <a href="https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20221128005451/en/"><ins>said in a statement</ins></a>. “From inception, BlockFi has worked to positively shape the cryptocurrency industry and advance the sector. BlockFi looks forward to a transparent process that achieves the best outcome for all clients and other stakeholders.”</p><p>BlockFi says that, as part of its restructuring, it will "focus on recovering all obligations owed to BlockFi by its counterparties, including FTX and associated corporate entities." However, it noted that recoveries from FTX are likely to be delayed, given that company's bankruptcy process. In addition, BlockFi says it has $256.9 million in cash on hand, which should provide “sufficient liquidity to support certain operations during the restructuring process," such as paying employee wages and continuing benefits.</p><p>In <a href="https://restructuring.ra.kroll.com/blockfi/Home-DocketInfo"><ins>a court filing</ins></a>, BlockFi estimated it had more than 100,000 creditors and consolidated liabilities of between $1 billion and $10 billion. Among the listed creditors are FTX (to which it owes $275 million in loan repayments) and the Securities and Exchange Commission, which it owes $30 million.</p><p>Earlier this year, BlockFi agreed to <a href="https://www.engadget.com/blockfi-sec-settlement-crypto-lender-203540418.html"><ins>pay $100 million to settle charges</ins></a> from the SEC and 32 states. The SEC claimed that BlockFi offered interest accounts without registering them under the Securities Act. The agency also found that the company made "false and misleading" claims related to the level of risk in its lending activity and loan portfolio.</p><p>Filing for Chapter 11 bankruptcy protection doesn't inherently mean a company is done for. The process allows a struggling business to keep trading while it restructures and looks for ways to pay back creditors. However, bankruptcy isn't easy to come back from, and BlockFi is just the latest in a long line of dominoes to fall in the precarious crypto industry.</p>

## The best Cyber Monday 2022 TV deals we could find
 - [https://www.engadget.com/best-cyber-monday-2022-tv-deals-we-could-find-153009196.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/best-cyber-monday-2022-tv-deals-we-could-find-153009196.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 15:30:09+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>Maybe you've been going back and forth about whether you should pick up a new TV while many are on sale for Cyber Monday. Undoubtably, now is a great time to do so if you want to save some money in the process. Cyber Monday TV deals are in full swing, and they discount a number of 4K and OLED sets from brands like Samsung, Sony, LG and others. While, yes, if you want an OLED set, you're still going to pay a premium for it, but most of these sale prices are much easier to stomach than the standard prices of high-end OLED sets. And if you're just looking for an upgraded 4K TV, there are plenty of great deals to choose from. ## Twitter spam obscures China COVID policy protest news
 - [https://www.engadget.com/twitter-spam-hides-china-covid-protests-152534633.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/twitter-spam-hides-china-covid-protests-152534633.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 15:25:34+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>You won't have much success finding news of China's growing protests if you search the country's larger cities on Twitter. As <em>TechCrunch</em><a href="https://techcrunch.com/2022/11/28/great-wall-of-porn-obscures-china-protest-news-on-twitter/">reports</a>, analysts have <a href="https://twitter.com/AirMovingDevice/status/1597034969293271040">noticed</a> a surge in bots peddling porn and gambling around these queries just as demonstrations flared in Beijing and other cities over the past three days in response to China's "zero-COVID" policies. The spam is making it harder to track the rallies, particularly for local activists who are using Twitter through a VPN to avoid Chinese government censorship of the protests on domestic social networks.</p><p>Twitter has effectively dissolved its communications team and hasn't officially commented on the matter. However, <em>The Washington Post</em><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2022/11/27/twitter-china-spam-protests/">notes</a> a Twitter employee told a researcher that the company is "working to resolve" the bot problem. It was easier to find word of the protests by late Sunday, but spam was still cluttering results. A former staffer told <em>The Post</em> that government-linked Twitter accounts have previously spammed en masse, but usually to attack individual accounts or small groups.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><div id="7aad9e1a97d94e879601a7b51643e01c"><blockquote class="twitter-tweet"><p dir="ltr" lang="en">Thread: Search for Beijing/Shanghai/other cities in Chinese on Twitter and you'll mostly see ads for escorts/porn/gambling, drowning out legitimate search results.<br />Data analysis in this thread suggests that there has been a *significant* uptick in these spam tweets. <a href="https://t.co/Ao46g2ILzf">pic.twitter.com/Ao46g2ILzf</a></p>— Air-Moving Device (@AirMovingDevice) <a href="https://twitter.com/AirMovingDevice/status/1597034969293271040?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw">November 28, 2022</a></blockquote></div><p>The protests largely grew in the wake of a deadly fire at an apartment in Xinjiang province's capital city Urumqi. Critics blamed the Chinese government's strict COVID-19 lockdown measures for delaying firefighters and otherwise contributing to deaths. <a href="https://www.engadget.com/apple-foxconn-iphone-plant-in-china-rocked-by-violent-protests-100639946.html">Working conditions at a Foxconn factory</a> in Zhengzhou, including concerns about inadequate COVID safety measures, also led to protests. The street action is rare in its intensity — some protesters have called on President Xi Jinping and other members of the Communist Party to resign. Those demands could easily lead to prison time in the country.</p><p>There are concerns that Elon Musk's <a href="https://www.engadget.com/twitter-done-with-job-cuts-blue-verified-062148989.html">aggressive job cuts</a> may have exacerbated the situation. <em>TechCrunch</em> pointed out that the entrepreneur <a href="https://twitter.com/yoyoel/status/1588657227035918337">laid off</a> Twitter's anti-propaganda team, leaving only the core moderation group. Where Twitter previously reacted quickly to China's attempts to <a href="https://www.engadget.com/2019-08-18-twitter-china-ads-attack-hong-kong-protesters.html">undercut Hong Kong protests</a>, it took days to begin curbing spam this time around. The company has resumed hiring, but it's not clear how much support the anti-misinformation unit will get.</p><p>The spike also challenges Musk's stance on bots. He tried to back out of the Twitter acquisition over claims the social network was <a href="https://www.engadget.com/elon-musk-accuses-twitter-of-fraud-fake-accounts-073225706.html">hiding the true number of fake accounts</a>. Spammers and other bogus users may now be more of a problem than they were before, if just because Twitter isn't as well-equipped to deal with the threat.</p>

## Apple Watch Ultra's powerful diving tools arrive with the Oceanic+ app
 - [https://www.engadget.com/apple-watch-ultra-oceanic-plus-dive-computer-app-144936455.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/apple-watch-ultra-oceanic-plus-dive-computer-app-144936455.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 14:49:36+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>Apple said the <a href="https://www.engadget.com/apple-watch-ultra-review-battery-life-compass-gps-hike-130055477.html">Watch Ultra</a> would be more useful for divers once a key app arrived, and that moment is finally here. Hush Outdoors and Apple have <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?merchantId=4130e2f0-a14f-4c5e-bdab-cd52ac7d8e79&amp;siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;merchantName=Apple&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsInN0b3JlSWQiOiI0MTMwZTJmMC1hMTRmLTRjNWUtYmRhYi1jZDUyYWM3ZDhlNzkiLCJsYW5kaW5nVXJsIjoiaHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuYXBwbGUuY29tL25ld3Nyb29tLzIwMjIvMTEvcmVhY2gtbmV3LWRlcHRocy13aXRoLXRoZS1vY2VhbmljLXBsdXMtYXBwLWFuZC1hcHBsZS13YXRjaC11bHRyYS8iLCJjb250ZW50VXVpZCI6ImVlNjU4MDI3LTIxNTgtNDBmYi1hNzZiLWE4YzUzZjVhZDdkMCJ9&amp;signature=AQAAAeOq5OcBOjZwcZOrOdFurXQXRiZm_-Ng2NWNOo2o7mdS&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.apple.com%2Fnewsroom%2F2022%2F11%2Freach-new-depths-with-the-oceanic-plus-app-and-apple-watch-ultra%2F">released</a> Oceanic+, effectively giving Ultra owners a recreation-oriented dive computer. The software tracks fundamentals like depth, no-decompression time (a figure used to set duration limits for given depths) and water temperature. The app is designed to be used without the touchscreen, and you can set compass headings using the action button. Even the haptic feedback is strong enough to be felt through a wetsuit.</p><p>You can plan dives to make the most of your trips, including the tides and currents. An after-dive review will show data that includes your water entry and exit locations. You'll find more information on your iPhone, such as depth graphs and the temperature ascent rate.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><figure><img alt="Oceanic+ app on Apple Watch Ultra" src="https://s.yimg.com/os/creatr-uploaded-images/2022-11/987ea6a0-6f2a-11ed-9ffd-fa608918ba85" style="height: 1440; width: 1920;" /><figcaption></figcaption><div class="photo-credit">Apple</div></figure><p>Basic Oceanic+ functionality such as depth, time and dive logging is free. You'll want to pay $10 per month or $80 per year for decompression tracking, location planning and other more advanced features. A $129 per year family plan allows access to five people. The app requires at least watchOS 9.1 as well as an iPhone 8 or later using iOS 16.1.</p><p>Apple is quick to caution that Oceanic+ isn't for professional scuba divers. This won't track remaining air like some dive computers, for example — the Apple Watch Ultra doesn't support transmitters that connect to your tank. This is strictly for enthusiast use, and only down to 130 feet. The watch can officially survive depths of 328 feet.</p><p>Even so, the launch could be important. This fulfills a promise Apple made in early September, and makes the Watch Ultra considerably more useful if you frequently plunge underwater. The timepiece launched with only basic depth tracking that wasn't much help if you wanted to avoid the bends or find your way back. While this won't replace dedicated hardware for particularly committed divers, it might save money if you wanted one watch you could wear both above and below the surface.</p>

## Meta fined €265 million over Facebook data scraping in the EU
 - [https://www.engadget.com/meta-fined-265-million-euros-over-data-scraping-142937633.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/meta-fined-265-million-euros-over-data-scraping-142937633.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 14:29:37+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>Meta has been hit with a €265 million ($277 million) fine for failing to prevent millions of Facebook users' mobile phone numbers and other data from being scraped and dumped online, <a href="https://www.independent.ie/business/technology/meta-fined-265m-in-facebook-data-scraping-case-that-exposed-millions-of-mobile-phone-numbers-42179037.html"><em>Independent.ie</em></a> has reported. It's the second fine levied by the Irish Data Protection Commission (DPC) in just the past few months, following a €405 million ($402 million at the time) penalty <a href="https://www.engadget.com/meta-fined-405-million-euro-instagram-privacy-161348122.html">issued in September</a>. In just the last 18 months, Meta has tallied nearly €1 billion in fines.&nbsp;</p><p>The penalty was issued in response to the leak of 533 million Facebook users' data reported in <a href="https://www.engadget.com/facebook-533-million-user-personal-data-leak-180156777.html">April last year</a>. That included phone numbers, birth dates, email addresses and locations, information that could be exploited in phishing and other attacks. The private information of sitting judges, prison officers, social workers, journalists and others were posted online, the DPC said.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>At the time, Meta blamed the attack on "bad actors," but Ireland's regulator said the company failed to comply with GDPR obligations of "data protection by design and default." It wrote in a <a href="https://www.dataprotection.ie/en/news-media/press-releases/data-protection-commission-announces-decision-in-facebook-data-scraping-inquiry">news release</a> that other data protection authorities in the EU "agreed with the decision of the DPC."&nbsp;</p><p>Meta confirmed to the <a href="https://www.wsj.com/articles/facebook-parent-meta-fined-276-million-in-europe-for-data-scraping-leak-11669640402"><em>The Wall Street Journal</em></a> that the flaw had been patched back in 2019. The company said that it will review DPC Ireland's decision, but has not yet decided whether to appeal. "Unauthorized data scraping is unacceptable and against our rules," the spokesperson added.&nbsp;</p><p>Last year, the DPC <a href="https://www.engadget.com/whatsapp-eu-fine-facebook-data-sharing-144749929.html">fined</a> Meta's WhatsApp €225 million ($267 million) for not providing details of how it shares European Union users' data with Facebook. It was also hit with a <a href="https://www.engadget.com/meta-facebook-gdpr-data-breach-eu-fine-173528015.html">€17 million ($18.6 million) fine</a> over 12 separate data breaches, and penalized €405 million ($402 million) for its handling of children’s privacy settings on Instagram.&nbsp;</p>

## WhatsApp's latest feature makes it easier to send messages to yourself
 - [https://www.engadget.com/whatsapp-now-lets-you-send-messages-to-yourself-124010198.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/whatsapp-now-lets-you-send-messages-to-yourself-124010198.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 12:40:10+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>WhatsApp has introduced a new feature that lets you send messages to yourself like reminders and shopping lists, parent Meta has confirmed with <a href="https://techcrunch.com/2022/11/28/whatsapp-rolls-out-a-feature-that-makes-it-easier-to-message-yourself/"><em>TechCrunch</em></a>. Called "Message Yourself," the feature was <a href="https://wabetainfo.com/whatsapp-is-testing-improvements-for-sending-messages-to-yourself-on-ios-and-android-beta/">first spotted by WaBetaInfo</a> several weeks ago as part of a beta test, but is now being rolled out globally to iOS and Android users in the coming weeks.</p><p>Once you get the update, you'll be able to see yourself at the top of the contacts list when creating new messages. Once you click on that, you'll be able to send yourself notes, reminders, shopping lists and anything else you might need to remember. The resulting notification, if enabled, could help make sure your self-note doesn't go unheeded. Users can also pin their Message Yourself chats to the top of a conversation list for easier access.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>Until now, you could only message yourself by creating a group with just you as a member or by using the apps "click to chat" feature, both inelegant solutions at best. Rival platform Signal already offers a feature called "Note to Self" that does much the same thing, though it's buried in your contacts list rather than being available at the top. As mentioned, you should see the feature in the next couple of weeks whether on Android or iOS.&nbsp;</p>

## The Morning After: Senator calls for an end to ‘failed Big Tech self-regulation’
 - [https://www.engadget.com/the-morning-after-senator-calls-for-an-end-to-failed-big-tech-self-regulation-121518897.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/the-morning-after-senator-calls-for-an-end-to-failed-big-tech-self-regulation-121518897.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 12:15:18+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>Senator Ed Markey of Massachusetts is calling on Congress to pass new legislation to rein in tech companies after Twitter boss Elon Musk ignored an information request. “Elon Musk could respond to my tweets but failed to respond to my letter by yesterday’s deadline and answer basic questions about Twitter verification,” Markey tweeted on Saturday.</p><p>The senator sent a letter on November 11th about Twitter’s paid account verification feature. Following the initial rollout, trolls could <a href="https://www.engadget.com/twitter-blue-verification-impersonation-disaster-203656712.html"><ins>impersonate</ins></a> celebrities, politicians and company brand accounts, the latter leading to real-world effects on stock prices.</p><p>Musk addressed one of Markey’s questions when he announced Twitter’s new verification system on Friday. It’ll feature manual authentication and different colored check marks for different types of users. "Gold check for companies, gray check for government, blue for individuals (celebrity or not) and all verified accounts will be manually authenticated before check activates," Musk said. He’s also said sign-ups have hit an <a href="https://www.engadget.com/twitter-user-signups-hit-all-time-high-says-elon-musk-180252792.html"><ins>all-time high</ins></a>.</p><p>– Mat Smith</p><p><em>The Morning After isn’t just a</em><a href="https://www.engadget.com/about/newsletter/"><em> newsletter</em></a><em> –  it’s also a daily podcast. Get our daily audio briefings, Monday through Friday, by</em><a href="https://www.engadget.com/2019-08-01-engadget-podcasts.html"><em> subscribing right here</em></a><em>.</em></p><p></p><h3>The biggest stories you might have missed</h3><ul><li><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/hitting-the-books-how-sex-changed-the-internet-samantha-cole-workman-publishing-153058910.html"><ins>Hitting the Books: Social media's long, pointless war against sex on the internet </ins></a></p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/half-life-alyx-levitation-available-to-download-202157601.html"><ins>‘Half-Life: Alyx’ mod adds four hours of single-player content</ins></a></p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/slow-horses-season-2-dead-lions-review-080042215.html"><ins>‘Slow Horses’ settles into a familiar but welcome groove</ins></a></p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/ferrari-vision-gran-turismo-7-december-3rd-222322992.html"><ins>Ferrari’s Vision hybrid race car arrives in ‘Gran Turismo 7’ on December 23rd</ins></a></p></li><li><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/internet-archive-pa-emulation-project-210328421.html"><ins>The Internet Archive’s PalmPilot Emulation project lets you relive tech history</ins></a></p></li></ul><p></p><h2><a href="https://www.engadget.com/fcc-officially-bans-telecom-and-video-surveillance-gear-from-several-chinese-companies-003040729.html">FCC bans telecom and video surveillance gear from Huawei and ZTE</a></h2><h3>The agency is implementing the rules from the 2021 Secure Equipment Act.</h3><a href="https://www.engadget.com/fcc-officially-bans-telecom-and-video-surveillance-gear-from-several-chinese-companies-003040729.html"><figure><img alt="TMA" src="https://s.yimg.com/os/creatr-uploaded-images/2022-11/b267cf90-6f09-11ed-bfd9-347b13472864" style="height: 450; width: 675;" /><figcaption></figcaption><div class="photo-credit">Getty Images</div></figure></a><p>The FCC announced it's officially implementing the Secure Equipment Act, which means some future equipment from Huawei, ZTE, Hytera, Hikvision and Dahua won't be authorized for sale in the US. Existing equipment from those companies, all listed under the FCC's Covered List, aren't affected by the law. Last year, the Biden administration signed into law the Secure Equipment Act, which aimed to block the authorization of network licenses from several Chinese companies whose hardware has been deemed a national security threat.</p><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/fcc-officially-bans-telecom-and-video-surveillance-gear-from-several-chinese-companies-003040729.html"><strong>Continue reading.</strong></a></p><p></p><h2><a href="https://www.engadget.com/nasa-orion-spacecraft-break-apollo-13-flight-record-172235996.html https://www.engadget.com/...">NASA’s Orion spacecraft breaks Apollo 13 flight record</a></h2><h3>The capsule traveled farther than any spacecraft designed to carry humans had before.</h3><a href="https://www.engadget.com/nasa-orion-spacecraft-break-apollo-13-flight-record-172235996.html https://www.engadget.com/..."><figure><img alt="TMA" src="https://s.yimg.com/os/creatr-uploaded-images/2022-11/b267cf90-6f09-11ed-b7ff-61a76861ddaf" style="height: 422; width: 675;" /><figcaption></figcaption><div class="photo-credit">NASA</div></figure></a><p>The Artemis 1 Orion crew vehicle has set a record for a NASA flight. On Saturday, Orion flew farther than any spacecraft designed to carry human astronauts had ever before, surpassing the previous record set by Apollo 13 back in 1970 – not that it was the aim of the mission. Funnily enough, it’s fitting that Artemis 1 was the one to do it. As Space.com points out, Apollo 13’s original flight plan didn’t call for a record-setting flight. It was only after a mid-mission explosion forced NASA to plot a new return course that Apollo 13’s Odyssey command module set the previous record at 248,655 miles (400,171 kilometers) from Earth.</p><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/nasa-orion-spacecraft-break-apollo-13-flight-record-172235996.html https://www.engadget.com/..."><strong>Continue reading.</strong></a></p><p></p><h2><a href="https://www.engadget.com/charles-darwin-full-correspondence-letters-online-233001600.html">Charles Darwin's full correspondence is now available online</a></h2><h3>You can read over 15,000 letters from the evolutionary science pioneer.</h3><h3></h3><p>The University of Cambridge has published all the evolutionary scientist's surviving correspondence online, including 400 letters that have either surfaced or are newly "reinterpreted." The searchable collection now covers over 15,000 letters written between 1822 and 1882, ranging from his influential time aboard the HMS Beagle to <em>On the Origin of Species</em> and his end-of-life reflections. The internet archive may even be the only way to see a fuller picture of Darwin's life. The university notes a print edition of his correspondence, due in early 2023, doesn't include letters that arrived too late to reach physical copies.</p><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/charles-darwin-full-correspondence-letters-online-233001600.html"><strong>Continue reading.</strong></a></p><p></p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><h2><a href="https://www.engadget.com/deepfake-porn-uk-ban-online-safety-bill-171007700.html https://www.engadget.com/...">UK aims to ban non-consensual deepfake porn</a></h2><h3>Critics say other aspects of the proposed legislation pose dangers to privacy and security.</h3><h3></h3><p>The UK government will amend its Online Safety Bill with measures designed to prohibit abuse of intimate images, whether or not they're real. If the bill becomes law as is, it will be illegal to share deepfake porn without the subject's consent. This would be the first ban on sharing deepfakes in the country, and if the law comes into effect, violating this rule could lead to a prison sentence. Critics have pushed back against certain aspects of the bill, including a revived plan to verify a person's age before permitting them to access adult content online.</p><p><a href="https://www.engadget.com/deepfake-porn-uk-ban-online-safety-bill-171007700.html https://www.engadget.com/..."><strong>Continue reading. </strong></a></p><p></p>

That effectively gives you a <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?merchantId=66ea567a-c987-4c2e-a2ff-02904efde6ea&amp;siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;merchantName=Amazon&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsInN0b3JlSWQiOiI2NmVhNTY3YS1jOTg3LTRjMmUtYTJmZi0wMjkwNGVmZGU2ZWEiLCJsYW5kaW5nVXJsIjoiaHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuYW1hem9uLmNvbS9kcC9CMEJDWEo4QkY0P209QVRWUERLSUtYMERFUiZyZWY9cHNwX3BjX2FfQTlPNzBFREVLQ09NMCZ0aD0xJnRhZz1nZGd0MGMtcC1vLWE2LTIwIiwiY29udGVudFV1aWQiOiIxMTczMmZkNi0wZGVkLTQ1YTItOTk1MC1mNDI1OTgyZTdjNmQifQ&amp;signature=AQAAAbYut_UCjtGhn5wuNNWSPbEBT3LzydJfY7NZGvVcs0eo&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2Fdp%2FB0BCXJ8BF4%3Fm%3DATVPDKIKX0DER%26ref%3Dpsp_pc_a_A9O70EDEKCOM0%26th%3D1">$100 discount</a> (33 percent) off the regular $300 price for today only — a great deal on a very good console.&nbsp;</p><a class="athena-button rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?merchantId=66ea567a-c987-4c2e-a2ff-02904efde6ea&amp;siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=shopnow-button&amp;merchantName=Amazon&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsInN0b3JlSWQiOiI2NmVhNTY3YS1jOTg3LTRjMmUtYTJmZi0wMjkwNGVmZGU2ZWEiLCJsYW5kaW5nVXJsIjoiaHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuYW1hem9uLmNvbS9kcC9CMEJDWEo4QkY0P209QVRWUERLSUtYMERFUiZyZWY9cHNwX3BjX2FfQTlPNzBFREVLQ09NMCZ0aD0xJnRhZz1nZGd0MGMtcC1vLWE3LTIwIiwiY29udGVudFV1aWQiOiIxMTczMmZkNi0wZGVkLTQ1YTItOTk1MC1mNDI1OTgyZTdjNmQifQ&amp;signature=AQAAAX6bhkH6Z1FRNCuMU8HyS5dwDtt5O2XrUbwI7_K6wRDU&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2Fdp%2FB0BCXJ8BF4%3Fm%3DATVPDKIKX0DER%26ref%3Dpsp_pc_a_A9O70EDEKCOM0%26th%3D1" id="77a3fbfdc6724154b75188da12e36b0f">Buy Xbox Series S at Amazon - $240 (with $40 credit) </a><p>When the Series S came out, we called it the "<a href="https://www.engadget.com/xbox-series-s-review-140027758.html">next-gen starter pack</a>" and gave it a solid 85 score. Even though it doesn't support gameplay in 4K, it plays incredibly smoothly and has a svelte look that will fit into any decor. Thanks to the FPS boost technology added to the Series S and X, <a href="https://support.xbox.com/en-US/help/games-apps/backward-compatibility/what-games-are-compatible-with-my-xbox">older games</a>, including many made for Xbox One, will look and perform better with faster frame rates.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>Unlike the Series X, the Series S only plays digital titles, with no slot to insert physical game media. It's a great option if you have an <a href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsImxhbmRpbmdVcmwiOiJodHRwczovL3d3dy54Ym94LmNvbS9lbi1VUy94Ym94LWdhbWUtcGFzcyIsImNvbnRlbnRVdWlkIjoiMDQxMGE1NzMtNjYxNy00Nzc1LWI0OTQtZjFiOWMxNmNjODkwIn0&amp;signature=AQAAAf6h867DmVjbkYUE0L8a23yP4wE-BuVvudvUVPJ4fMaU&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.xbox.com%2Fen-US%2Fxbox-game-pass&amp;uuid=MO6cZo8qp5PIuGXG2692">Xbox Game Pass</a> membership, though, which costs $10 per month for the Console tier, and $15 per month for the Ultimate tier. Either level unlocks a library with hundreds of game to download and play, while also granting discounts to many titles you might want to buy outright.</p><p>Another caveat is that the Series S has less SSD storage, with 512GB on-board compared to the 1TB for the Series X. If you like to keep plenty of titles on hand, you'll either need to shuffle them between the main disk and <a class="rapid-with-clickid" storage</a>, or purchase Seagate's <a class="rapid-with-clickid" href="https://shopping.yahoo.com/rdlw?merchantId=66ea567a-c987-4c2e-a2ff-02904efde6ea&amp;siteId=us-engadget&amp;pageId=1p-autolink&amp;featureId=text-link&amp;merchantName=Amazon&amp;custData=eyJzb3VyY2VOYW1lIjoiV2ViLURlc2t0b3AtVmVyaXpvbiIsInN0b3JlSWQiOiI2NmVhNTY3YS1jOTg3LTRjMmUtYTJmZi0wMjkwNGVmZGU2ZWEiLCJsYW5kaW5nVXJsIjoiaHR0cHM6Ly93d3cuYW1hem9uLmNvbS9TZWFnYXRlLVN0b3JhZ2UtRXhwYW5zaW9uLVNvbGlkLVN0YXRlL2RwL0IwOEszUzZXSk0vcmVmPXNyXzFfMz9jcmlkPUVaWVFHSkhFSlg5RSZrZXl3b3Jkcz1zZWFnYXRlJTJCeGJveCUyQmV4cGFuc2lvbiZxaWQ9MTY2OTYzMjU1MiZzcHJlZml4PXNlYWdhdGUlMkJ4Ym94JTJCZXhwYW5zaW9uJTJDYXBzJTJDNTA1JnNyPTgtMyZ1ZmU9YXBwX2RvJTNBYW16bjEuZm9zLjA4ZjY5YWMzLWZkM2QtNGI4OC1iY2EyLTg5OTdlNDE0MTBiYiZ0aD0xJnRhZz1nZGd0MGMtcC1vLWE2LTIwIiwiY29udGVudFV1aWQiOiIxMTczMmZkNi0wZGVkLTQ1YTItOTk1MC1mNDI1OTgyZTdjNmQifQ&amp;signature=AQAAAXfHs6cAVu2QxTYoqKXfyRMbAYNi0qlQn1PqtmsI41PM&amp;gcReferrer=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amazon.com%2FSeagate-Storage-Expansion-Solid-State%2Fdp%2FB08K3S6WJM%2Fref%3Dsr_1_3%3Fcrid%3DEZYQGJHEJX9E%26keywords%3Dseagate%252Bxbox%252Bexpansion%26qid%3D1669632552%26sprefix%3Dseagate%252Bxbox%252Bexpansion%252Caps%252C505%26sr%3D8-3%26ufe%3Dapp_do%253Aamzn1.fos.08f69ac3-fd3d-4b88-bca2-8997e41410bb%26th%3D1">$200 expansion card</a>. ## Twitter data leak exposes over 5.4 million accounts
 - [https://www.engadget.com/twitter-data-for-54-million-users-leaked-online-095040426.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/twitter-data-for-54-million-users-leaked-online-095040426.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 09:50:40+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p>Earlier this year, Twitter <a href="https://www.engadget.com/twitter-confirms-july-data-exposure-173208043.html">confirmed</a> that the private user data for 5.4 million users was stolen due to an API vulnerability, but the company said it had "no evidence" that it was exploited. Now, all of those accounts have been exposed on a hacker form, <a href="https://www.bleepingcomputer.com/news/security/54-million-twitter-users-stolen-data-leaked-online-more-shared-privately/"><em>BleepingComputer</em></a> has reported. On top of that, an additional 1.4 million Twitter profiles for suspended users was reportedly shared privately, and an even larger data dump with the data of "tens of millions" of other users may have come from the same vulnerability.</p><p>The owner of hacking forum called Breached told <em>BleepingComputer</em> that it was responsible for exploiting the  weakness (originally obtained from another hacker called "Devil") and dumping the user records. It said that it also obtained 1.4 million Twitter profiles for suspended accounts, obtained via another API, but only shared those privately among a few individuals.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>On top of all that, security expert Chad Loder has revealed that tens of millions more Twitter records may have been collected using the same API. Once again, data collected may include private phone numbers along with public information. Loder posted a redacted sample on <a href="https://kolektiva.social/@chadloder/109406380942373215">Mastodon</a>, as he was <a href="https://www.reddit.com/r/EnoughMuskSpam/comments/z4h24r/elon_just_suspended_chad_loder_a_antifascist/">banned</a> on Twitter several days ago for unknown reasons. It could contain over 17 million records, <em>BleepingComputer</em> was told.</p><p>The breaches leaked users' private phone numbers and email addresses, which could be used for phishing and other scams. That information could also be exploited to uncover identities from private Twitter accounts. As usual, be very wary of any suspicious emails or texts claiming to come from Twitter — and if you're thinking about using two-factor authentication, now would be a good time.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>

## ‘Slow Horses’ settles into a familiar, but welcome, groove
 - [https://www.engadget.com/slow-horses-season-2-dead-lions-review-080042215.html?src=rss](https://www.engadget.com/slow-horses-season-2-dead-lions-review-080042215.html?src=rss)
 - RSS feed: https://www.engadget.com/rss.xml
 - date published: 2022-11-28 08:00:42+00:00
 - Starred: False

<p><em>Slow Horses</em> was something of a slow-burning surprise when its first season launched back in April. It was yet another Apple TV hit whose marketing hadn’t done well enough to connect with audiences, relying instead on word of mouth. What viewers found, however, was a low-stakes spy drama with the sort of pulpy, throwback thrills that you rarely see in our more self-serious age. Mixed with a shot or two of black comedy, and it made for a surprisingly gripping package I felt <a href="https://www.engadget.com/slow-horses-apple-tv-plus-160047710.html"><ins>compelled to rave about back in April</ins></a>.</p><p>The show’s second season, which returns to Apple TV+ on December 2nd, carries on in that vein, albeit with less of the show’s trademark humor. It focuses, once again, on the staff members of Slough House, the closest thing MI5 has to purgatory for disgraced intelligence officers. Led by the “colorful” Jackson Lamb, the Slow Horses are often left doing administrative donkeywork nobody else thinks is worth doing. Of course, you wouldn’t have a series if the misfits weren’t frequently embroiled in the grander machinations of the intelligence community.</p><span id="end-legacy-contents"></span><p>Season Two is based on<em> Dead Lions</em>, the second in Herron’s series of <em>Slough House</em> novels, and focuses on Lamb’s investigation of the death of a former officer. Apple’s usual ban on spoilers means that, of the plot, I can only say that it features “long-buried Cold War secrets” which “threaten to bring carnage to the streets of London.” Oh, and that “when a liaison with Russian villains takes a fatal turn, our hapless heroes must overcome their individual failings and raise their spy game in a race to prevent a catastrophic incident.”</p><p>We pick up shortly after the first season, with the Horses frustrated that their heroics haven’t led to better things. Instead, the team has been bolstered with Shirley Dander (Aimee-Ffion Edwards) and Marcus Longridge (Kadiff Kirwan) and put back on regular duties. That has, understandably, left River Cartwright (Jack Lowden) in something of a funk. But when a former agent is found dead on a bus, it suddenly piques Jackson Lamb’s (Gary Oldman) interest enough to return to work in the field.</p><p>Given that the first two six-episode seasons were shot in a single run, it’s no surprise that the show expects you to recall much of what happened in the first run. But, despite the continuous production, there’s a big tonal shift here, with the show getting darker and dropping some of its trademark wit and humor. And, I’ll be honest, the running gag about Jackson Lamb’s lack of personal hygiene and non-stop farting starts to get a bit thin by the end.</p><p>Fans of the books will already know <em>why</em> the series takes a darker turn, although I found some of the twists were initially a bit lightweight. Maybe years of watching series where nothing we see can be believed meant I was always waiting for a non-existent second shoe to drop. None exist here in the Slow Horses universe, and when you see some beloved characters go, uh, to places you might not expect, be mindful that none of it is for show.</p><p>It’s not a show that you can watch with one eye on your phone, but it’s so briskly paced that if you blink, you might lose your place. I’d consider myself a close watcher of things, but even I found myself having to pause to work out which sinister Russian emigre was which. It doesn’t help that while you can see where all of the various plotlines are heading, their collision is a little predictable. But I’m nitpicking, and this isn’t the sort of show you need to unpick for hours on end on Reddit – just repeat to yourself it’s just a show, and you should really just relax.</p><p>And Slow Horses’ second season really belongs to Rosalind Eleazar (Guy) and Saskia Reeves (Standish), who are both given time and space to grow their characters. The former carries much of the major narrative this time around, while the latter again shows how much steel is buried underneath Standish’s downtrodden personae. But the show is democratic enough to give every character a grace note or two during the explosive, and gripping, finale.</p><p><em>Slow Horses season two will launch on Apple TV+ on Friday, December 2nd, with two new episodes, with subsequent episodes appearing every Friday through December 30th. A third and fourth season has already been greenlit.</em></p>
